India Boycotts Japanese Goods 52

Special Tax Increased on Cotton Cloth Imports

Japan's Anti-British Sentiment Continues to Grow

Shimla: The Indian government announced that the minimum emergency special tax on plain, undyed cotton cloth not manufactured in the United Kingdom will be increased from 50% to 75% ad valorem. This measure is due to the depreciation of the Japanese yen and the intense competition of Japanese goods in India, which has affected the Indian cotton cloth industry and several other industries. The announcement mentioned the inapplicability of the 1904 India-Japan Commercial Treaty, but the Indian government reaffirmed its willingness to discuss the current situation in order to resolve the problem. (7th Reuters Dispatch)

Tokyo: The increase in import duties on Japanese cloth announced by the Shimla government has caused great indignation among Japanese businessmen. Coupled with the anti-Japanese movement by the British cotton goods industry, the anti-British sentiment in Japan is growing stronger. Japanese newspapers are supporting domestic industrialists and condemning the partiality of British merchants. However, the political circles remain calm, believing that the World Economic Conference is about to open, and trade talks between Britain and Japan will also be realized. The British government will definitely use its restraining power. (7th Reuters Dispatch)

Tokyo: The Ministry of Foreign Affairs will discuss countermeasures after receiving a detailed report on the issue of India's increase in cotton cloth tariffs and will lodge a protest with the Indian government. Tsuda, President of Kanebo Spinning, said that while Japan is working to cooperate with Britain to resolve trade issues, the Indian government suddenly and arbitrarily increased tariffs, which is a joint British-Indian effort to exclude Japanese goods. This increase in tariffs can be regarded as an ultimatum from Britain and India to Japanese cotton merchants. We have no choice but to consider the final means. Kawaguchi, representative of the Japan-India Economic Association, said that there is no denying that the Lancashire cotton merchants of Britain are behind India's increase in tariffs. India is using the pretext of protecting its industries to exclude Japanese goods, and the Netherlands, Italy, and Germany are also affected. (7th Jiji News Agency Dispatch)

Tokyo: Today at 1:00 PM, the Textile Federation held a special committee meeting to discuss countermeasures regarding India's tax increase. After discussion, the Textile Federation Committee will be convened again on the 8th to determine the attitude of the textile industry. Under the current circumstances, it seems to advocate the issue of the Anglo-Japanese trade agreement, and on the other hand, it will reject the hypocritical attitude of Britain. Therefore, the general opinion on the Anglo-Japanese trade agreement is to kick it away. (7th Dentsu Dispatch)

Japanese Government Manages Exports to Ease Dumping 53

Tokyo: The Commercial Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has decided to manage Japanese exports. It is expected that the Emperor will issue an order to manage them without waiting for the discussion of the next cabinet. This plan is to prevent Japanese merchants in foreign markets from taking advantage of currency depreciation to implement dumping policies. (7th Reuters Dispatch)

The League of Nations Advisory Committee Passes Measures to Not Recognize Puppet Organizations 55

Refuse to Participate in Various International Conferences and Conventions

Separately Notified to Member States and Non-Member States

Geneva: Today, the League of Nations Advisory Committee unanimously passed the report of the subcommittee on the implementation measures for not recognizing the "Manchukuo" puppet organization. The committee met at 10:05 AM in the Secretary-General's office, chaired by Norwegian representative Lange. It was also decided to immediately send this report to all relevant countries, including the United States, in the form of a circular. The proposal to ban the shipment of arms and other issues previously raised were not discussed today, nor was a firm date set for the next meeting. There were many absentees among the committee members today. Representatives from Turkey, Poland, Portugal, Panama, Canada, Hungary, and the Irish Free State were not present. Among the representatives present, the United States was represented by Wilson, the United Kingdom by Cadogan, Germany by Fonkeller, and France by Pougin. (7th National News Agency Dispatch)

Geneva: The League of Nations Advisory Committee sent a notice to the governments of various countries regarding the non-recognition of puppet organizations, which mentioned ① the issue of the "Manchukuo" puppet organization participating in various international conferences, postal affairs, and postage stamps; ② international non-recognition of the puppet organization's currency; ③ how to deal with the issue of foreign concessions and personnel dispatches in Manchuria arising from recognition; ④ passports and consular status; ⑤ the application of the import and export certification system stipulated in the 1925 Geneva Opium Conference and the 1931 Disarmament Conference. The above notice was sent to all member states of the League of Nations, as well as non-member states that are signatories to the Kellogg-Briand Pact or the Nine-Power Treaty. The Advisory Committee believes that although it is only responsible for providing recommendations to the governments of member states, based on the League of Nations General Assembly's hope that the signatories of the above two treaties will also be consistent with member states in their actions and attitudes when necessary, it is also notified together. (7th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Montreux, Switzerland: The International Federation of Organizations Supporting the League of Nations held a plenary session yesterday. Full Text of Japan's Reply to the United States 58

Agreeing in Principle with Feigned Courtesy

Attaching Reservations with Ill Intent

Tokyo: The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs passed the original draft of its reply to the US President's peace application at yesterday's cabinet meeting. At 7:00 PM, Foreign Minister Uchida telegraphed Ambassador Debuchi, who forwarded it to Phillips through Undersecretary of State. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs published the full text today as follows:

It has always been the basic policy of the Empire to contribute to the maintenance of world peace and the promotion of human welfare. In order to make the World Economic Conference and the Disarmament Conference successful, the Empire Government accepts with sincerity the encouragement of the US President to understand its intentions. Regarding the World Economic Conference recently held in London, the Empire Government is determined to cooperate with the governments of various countries in resolving the world economic downturn and increasing the welfare of the people of all countries. Regarding the Disarmament Conference, the Empire Government has great concern and is still doing its utmost to help achieve its goals. The intentions of the Empire Government, I believe, are in complete agreement with the noble aspirations of the President, whose purpose is to maintain world peace. As for the various stages mentioned in the President's communique, concrete opinions will be presented at any time as necessary. The Empire Government earnestly hopes that the above two major conferences will quickly reach a fair and reasonable solution, so that the world can escape the difficult situation it is currently encountering. (7th China Alliance Dispatch)

Planning to Have a Plan to Increase the Price of Silver 61

Roosevelt Steamer: The US delegation to the Economic Conference indicated today that the US President had informally agreed with politicians from several countries during talks at the White House the other day on the use of silver as a reserve for central banks. According to US representative Pittman, this informal and non-binding understanding will be submitted to the Economic Conference for discussion. He hopes that one of the results of its adoption in the future will be to stipulate a worldwide gold-silver ratio. Currently, the understanding does not yet extend to the issue of the ratio of the two precious metals. Its purpose is only to conserve gold. It is planned to stipulate that 25% of the US banknote reserves be gold and 5% be silver. The clothing country also handles it in the same way, but the gold-silver ratio should be slightly different. Central banks of various countries can stabilize the price of silver according to this plan. Even if the market price of silver still inevitably fluctuates slightly, it is not difficult for various banks to equalize the market by buying and selling silver, so that the rise and fall of the price of silver are always within the prescribed limits. If the price of silver falls too much, the central bank can purchase silver, so that the actual amount reaches 5% of the amount of banknotes issued. If the price of silver rises too much, the central bank can sell silver to stabilize the market. According to this method, the use of silver is broad, and its price can be raised slightly compared to the present. Mr. Pitt hopes that the price of silver may be raised to a level that is profitable for silver producers, but he is still unable to say for sure whether a gold-silver ratio can be adopted at the meeting in the future. Moreover, even the understanding between President Roosevelt and the politicians of various countries is not an agreement to adopt this plan, but only recognizes it as an acceptable basis for discussion. (6th National News Agency Dispatch)

British Debt to the US is About to Expire 62

Whether to Pay or Not is Still Undecided

Eagerly Awaiting the US to Provide a Way Out

London: The British Cabinet is scheduled to convene a special meeting on Friday to discuss the payment of debt to the US, which is due on June 15. The government expects that the US will have a statement on the war debt issue on that day. (7th Reuters Dispatch)

London: The question of whether or not the UK will pay the June installment of debt to the US still seems to be largely undecided. Although the payment date is only eight days away, the final decision has not yet been made. The British Parliament is scheduled to reopen on June 13, just two days before the payment is due. It is expected that the Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain will announce the government's decision to Parliament at that time. (7th Reuters Dispatch)

Washington: People at the White House claimed that as of now, the US government has not received any proposals from the debtor countries regarding the issue of resolving the war debt due on June 15. According to news from the UK, regarding the debt due on June 15, the British Cabinet must first know what the US expects of the UK before it can make any decision. US officials are quite surprised by this news and said that when the Hoover moratorium was passed by Congress, Congress voted on a resolution stipulating that war debts should not be reduced or cancelled. Roosevelt therefore did not make any suggestions to the debtor countries, but stated that he was prepared to consider any proposals. Since the debtor countries have not made any proposals, the US government can only maintain its position and wait quietly for the payment due on June 15. Moreover, the US Agricultural Relief Act contains provisions allowing debtor countries to repay part of their debt in silver. After the devaluation of the US dollar, the debtor countries have also indirectly benefited. The government is eager to understand the attitude of the various debtor countries, because the US Treasury needs a huge sum of 100 million yuan on June 15 to repay public debt and plans to issue short-term treasury bills to cope with it. The amount of treasury bills will depend on the payment situation of the various debtor countries. (6th Havas Dispatch)

Report of the Purchasing Committee in London 65

London The Financial Times today published an article criticizing the 1932 report of the Chinese government's Purchasing Committee in London. In that year, the committee used 550,000 pounds in British currency, and the total expenditure has now reached 750,000 pounds, with 3.7 million pounds remaining, ready to purchase British-made goods. The newspaper emphasized that this move is of great value from an occupational point of view. The newspaper also mentioned the matter of attracting Chinese students to study in England, stating that American industries have greatly benefited from Chinese students studying in the United States, because when they return to their country after completing their studies, they tend to purchase machinery that they are familiar with. If England were to follow America's example, it would certainly be able to promote the sale of British products. The committee's report has now been sent to China, accompanied by an article from Guo Taiqi, the Chinese Minister to England, as Guo is the chairman of the committee. The report details the various matters handled by the committee in accordance with the exchange of documents between China and Britain in 1930 regarding the use of the British portion of the Boxer Indemnity, and explains that the chairman went to Geneva on official business, so all affairs were temporarily presided over by the Acting Chargé d'affaires Chen. In that year, the committee held several meetings of the technical and financial subcommittees, as well as two plenary sessions. (7th Reuters Dispatch)

Progress of the Disarmament Conference 66

Managing Privately Manufactured Arms

Another Major Point of Contention Resolved

Geneva The United States has fully agreed to France's request for the issuance of licenses and strict management of privately manufactured arms. Another major point of contention within the General Disarmament Commission has been resolved. When France initially proposed this, it was highly doubtful whether the United States would agree. Until today, the French representative repeatedly stated that France's signature on the Disarmament Convention would depend on whether private companies could be strictly managed. The US representative, Davis, then declared that the United States was prepared to accept this proposal. This move by the Americans can be seen as a change in their consistent stance, as according to the French plan, the export and manufacture of arms will be subject to strict management. This proposal will now be included in the draft of the Disarmament Convention. It is expected that Britain will not object, as Britain's arms exports have always been managed by the government. The General Commission will probably adjourn within this week, while the drafting committee will continue its work. (6th National Telegram)

Contents of the Four-Power Pact 67

Italy, England, and France Prepare to Sign

But Germany Still Holds Reservations

Paris The semi-official summary of the Four-Power Pact is as follows: The preamble states that the main purpose is to give greater effect to the procedures stipulated in the Covenant of the League of Nations, and adds an agreement that the four powers shall not infringe upon the rights of other countries. The treaty has five articles: ㈠ England, France, Italy, and Germany agree to cooperate; ㈡ stipulates the exchange of views regarding the application of the provisions of the League of Nations Covenant, especially Article 10 (maintaining the territorial status quo), Article 16 (sanctions against aggression), and Article 19 (revision of treaties); ㈢ stipulates that if the Disarmament Conference fails, the four powers must consult with each other to seek a solution to the pending issues; ㈣ the four powers may consider economic issues in Europe in which they have a common interest; ㈤ stipulates that this treaty is valid for ten years, and if no notice of termination is given at the end of the eighth year, the treaty may be extended for another ten years. (7th Reuters Dispatch)

Rome It seems difficult to know within a few hours whether all four powers will participate in the pact. Germany has requested that the preamble of the pact be slightly modified. The French ambassador to Italy, Jouvenel, has now sent the German request to Paris for instructions. Rome hopes that Germany's formal objections to the pact will not prevent it from being signed today. Generally, people are anxiously awaiting Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's declaration in the Senate. The Italian Prime Minister must wait until all objections to the pact have been eliminated before he can make a declaration in the Senate. (7th Havas Dispatch)

Berlin According to political sources, the German government must wait until tonight to decide on the issue of joining the Four-Power Pact, because Premier Hitler is returning to Berlin today, and Minister Nuerath and Aviation Minister Göring have already returned to Berlin. (7th Havas Dispatch)

Berlin The revised draft of the Four-Power Pact has been received here today and is currently being closely reviewed. The authorities have not yet announced their attitude. According to reliable sources, the original draft has been greatly modified, almost losing its original appearance. (6th National Telegram)

Rome Judging from Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's speech at today's Senate meeting, the Four-Power Pact of England, France, Germany, and Italy seems likely to be concluded within the day. According to the Italian Prime Minister, negotiations have reached a stage where the pact is sure to be concluded in a way that is imaginable. If necessary, he will speak tomorrow. At the same time, the Paris cabinet today instructed the French ambassador to Italy to accept the current draft, which is also acceptable to Britain. It is expected that a notice of Germany's agreement will also be received soon, at which time the pact can be formally established. (7th Reuters Dispatch)

London Germany still has reservations about the Four-Power Pact because the content of the pact is completely different from the original draft proposed by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, especially because it does not contain satisfactory clauses regarding Germany's demand for equality, and may refuse to sign it. (7th Reuters Dispatch)

Paris The date for the completion of the Four-Power Pact proposed by Mussolini to guarantee peace in Europe is not far away, because England, Italy, and France have already accepted the pact, and Germany may not openly oppose it. It is said that Article 3 of the pact, which relates to disarmament, is extremely moderate in its new form, merely stating that if disarmament fails, the signatory countries will meet to discuss the situation. According to a Reuters dispatch from Berlin, the news that the French government had agreed to sign the pact arrived in Berlin too late, so the stock exchange was not affected. According to opinions in Berlin official circles, the Italian Prime Minister's plan has been repeatedly revised by France and has lost its original nature. (6th Reuters Dispatch)

Former Greek Prime Minister Escapes Assassination 79

His Wife Hit by Four Bullets, Chauffeur Dies

▲ National Telegram, 7th, Athens: Former Greek Prime Minister Venizelos and his wife were traveling by car out of the city today when they were suddenly shot at nine kilometers from Athens. Mrs. Venizelos was hit by four bullets, but all were minor injuries. The chauffeur was also slightly injured. One of the guards was fatally wounded and died shortly after. The assailant is believed to be a relative of someone executed during Venizelos's term in office. The assassination was clearly planned in detail. After discovering that the Venizelos couple would be traveling in the countryside today, they waited on the road in a car. When their car drove between the Venizelos couple's car and the escort car, they immediately opened fire on Venizelos, firing more than sixteen bullets. Venizelos quickly hid under the car and tried to pull his wife down with him, but unfortunately, she had already been hit by four bullets, but none were fatal. Afterwards, the police were immediately called to pursue and arrest the assailant, but they had already driven into the countryside and have not yet been apprehended. An examination of the car revealed that the seats had been hit by a total of twelve bullets. Venizelos's escape from harm can be described as extremely close. After the incident, the chauffeur immediately drove the car back to the city and sent Mrs. Venizelos to the hospital to remove the bullets. Mrs. Venizelos was still able to sleep peacefully in the evening, and it seems that there will be no problems. Upon hearing the report, the police immediately investigated and arrested communist leaders, because Venizelos had severely suppressed the communist party during his term in office and executed many people, so it is expected that this was a retaliatory conspiracy by communists.

▲ Reuters, 7th, Athens: Greek politician Venizelos, who has served as prime minister eight times and has a high reputation, was shot at last night while returning to Athens from Kifissia with his wife. His wife and the chauffeur were injured, but Venizelos himself was unharmed. It is reported that Venizelos, who is now sixty-nine years old, resigned as prime minister due to the violent coup carried out by General Hadjikyriakos, and was succeeded by Tsaldaris. He married his current wife in 1921.

Japanese Publishing Industry Discusses the Dangers of Military Clique Dictatorship 80

Army Ministry General Staff Controls Government Meetings

If There Is No Resistance to the Military Clique, Japan's Future Is Worrying

Is Economic Power Enough to Defeat First-Class Powers?

Japan Should Abandon the Inferior Mentality of the Orient

The Yulin Daily's Tokyo correspondent reports that the "Liberation Magazine" published in June will contain two very interesting essays. Reading them reveals that the Japanese do not fully agree with the actions of their military clique and its followers. The reporter, with the kind permission of an employee of the magazine, was shown the contents of the two articles so that readers of the Xiaolin Daily could see them. There are inconsistencies in the writing of the two articles, which shows that the censor has made deletions and modifications. The main points of the two articles are recorded below:

One article, written by Arahata, discusses the resignation of Foreign Minister Arita, which was actually due to disagreements with Foreign Minister Uchida regarding the handling of the China issue and the Japan-Manchuria-Russia negotiations. The article states that the discord among the authorities in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is not a matter of one day or two. As the issue of Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations emerged, this conflict became more acute. Most of the senior officials in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs disagreed with Japan's declaration of withdrawal. Those who were solely under the command of the military clique were not. The conflict between the military and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is well known. At the beginning of the Manchurian Incident, the two sides were unable to tolerate each other. The military could no longer tolerate Shidehara's moderate diplomatic tactics, and drew their swords and declared a public break with him. This is why Shidehara retreated when he saw the opportunity. The author ridicules Matsuoka's final set of tricks in Geneva, which is to say that Japan is now the first line of defense against the possibility of China's redization. Matsuoka also said that if the League of Nations puts Japan in an isolated position, then Annam, India, and Egypt will not be able to safely remain under the power of imperialism. His words are foolish and laughable, and fully reveal Japan's entire policy towards Manchuria. The author's intention is that the Manchurian affairs actually show us that Japan's foreign policy is a transformed domestic policy. Since the European War, military preparations have been repeatedly reduced, and the power of the Ministry of the Army has greatly weakened. The power of the various political parties has continued to grow, resulting in a relative disadvantage. Therefore, the military has devoted all its efforts to resisting the successive foreign ministers, and Shidehara's diplomatic policy, which advocated cooperation with Europe and the United States to reduce the burden of military preparations, was especially opposed by the military. The steps to force Japan to withdraw from the League of Nations are actually nothing more than seeking to maintain the political power that the military clique temporarily enjoys today. The article concludes by saying that the foreign policy of the Army General Staff (Arahata did not mention this organization, because the censor did not allow it, so Arahata only used a certain organization to replace it, but it is clear where its intention lies.) now controls the government, parliament, and all speaking organs of Japan, and has transformed Foreign Minister Uchida from a soft rubber doll into a steel robot. The military clique not only monopolizes diplomatic power, but also draws huge sums of money from an unprecedented budget to expand military preparations. If the Japanese people do not quickly awaken and unite to resist, then Japan is in danger of being tossed about by the wind and rain. Another article, written by Yonebito, wonders whether the people of the country really know that they are currently encountering a serious difficulty, not only actually confronting one or two countries, but also confronting the whole world. However, few journalists or publishers with a little reputation have the courage to firmly oppose the government's current policy at this important turning point in the country's diplomacy, and to inform the people of the crisis of continuing this kind of radical policy. It is truly regrettable that even if one or two journalists have this "dangerous thought," no newspaper dares to disclose it. Although, according to what he knows for sure, it cannot be said that all Japanese people agree with the current so-called national policy. For example, Osaki is one of those who firmly oppose it. (It is reported that Osaki has been a member of parliament since Japan established a party government, and has once served as Minister of Justice. He has lived in England for a long time and has just returned to the country.) Furthermore, Mogi, the former chairman of Yokohama Mogi Company, also greatly doubts whether the authorities' current policies are well-considered. He believes that as a result of the development of imperialism, Europe has already been cleared, and in Asia and other places, it is being slowly cleared by the United Kingdom and the United States. Japan is once again trying to implement an extremely evil new form of imperialism on the East Asian continent. He believes that Japan, with nations such as China and India that are trying to rise up as neighbors, is currently in an extremely difficult position, and its actions must be extremely cautious so as not to leave regrets for the future. He asks whether it is wise to establish a Monroe Doctrine in East Asia to resist the regionalism of the natural development between nations, and doubts whether this kind of Monroe Doctrine and radical policy will be a reaction to world peace. He believes that as China and India are progressing along the path of capitalism, Japan's establishment of this kind of Monroe Doctrine, even if the world powers stand by and watch, is not known whether it will be beneficial to Japan. He also said that Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations at this time can be seen as Japan's diplomacy confronting world diplomacy and world public opinion. This move will not help to truly resolve the disputes between China and Japan, and while China remains in the League of Nations, he actually doubts whether Japan can favorably resolve the disputes between China and Japan by following the current policy. In practice, is it feasible? He then asks whether Japan can isolate itself from the rest of the world, whether it can continue to ignore the Kellogg-Briand Pact

and the Nine-Power Treaty indefinitely, and whether it can implement its continental policy as it pleases, regardless of others. He doubts this deeply, speculating that once Japan is forced to fight against a well-equipped country, its current isolated position is tantamount to fighting the whole world. Japan may be able to win a temporary victory, but the European War has already shown us that modern warfare is determined by economic power and endurance. I sincerely hope that those who believe that Japan can defeat truly first-class powers will pay attention to this. The authorities in charge have undoubtedly conducted a detailed investigation into the country's economic strength, but even with this economic strength, can they be sure that it can definitely support it for a long time without fatigue, or do they think that Japan's industry can only obtain raw materials from Manchuria and is enough to be self-sufficient? But who can prove the reliability of this statement? He believes that there are now those who do not hope for war, but warns those in Japan who want to fight that they must be prepared for the disaster of land sinking before they can do so. He believes that as a result of Japan's war, it will only impoverish its people and exhaust its wealth, leading to the complete collapse of the existing social order. Yonebito finally advocates cooperation between China and Japan to break the current situation of warlord separatism in China, believing that the ideal Sino-Japanese relationship can only be achieved when the economic activities of the two major nations can respect each other, need each other, and have considerable understanding. And he admits that the realization of this ideal Sino-Japanese relationship will take at least several decades. During this period, Japan should strive to cooperate with other nations more sincerely than before, and completely abandon the inferior mentality of the Orient.

Japanese Military Withdrawal Is Quite Slow 81

(Summary)

If There Is Sincerity, the Withdrawal Should Be Expedited

After the signing of the Sino-Japanese armistice agreement, our army has complied with the agreement and withdrawn separately. The various armies have gathered in Pingxiao, and will soon be demobilized and return to their original defenses. A portion of the Northeast Army has been transferred to Zhuozhou and other places on the Pinghan Line. The rest of the main force will also be divided into defense zones and stationed in appropriate locations. The Japanese army currently stationed on the Jixian line is the Hattori Brigade. The 16th Division of Puqi is stationed in Fengrun, Baodi, Sanhe, and other places. The 8th Division of Nishi Yoshiichi is stationed in the Miyun area. The area of Sanhe and Miyun is the area where the main force of the Japanese army is concentrated. There are not many Japanese troops on the front of the Beining Railway. Near Lutai, there are only puppet troops led by Li Jichun and Zhao Lei, totaling about two to three thousand people. The Japanese army's withdrawal is divided into three steps: first, the heavy artillery is withdrawn, then the baggage is withdrawn, and finally the infantry can be withdrawn. Although Japan has claimed to be withdrawing troops in recent days, only a portion has been withdrawn from Fengrun, Baodi, Yutian, and other places. Others are still claiming to be measuring and transporting baggage and heavy artillery, and there is no intention to withdraw far away. It is said that because of the continuous rain in recent days, the roads are muddy, and each division of the Japanese army's heavy artillery has about five or sixty doors, plus the attached bulky military supplies, the number is also quite large, and transportation is difficult. This may be the actual situation, and it is not known. Although the demobilization of our army is in active preparation, the war-time equipment is scheduled to be completed by the 16th of this month. However, whether it will be implemented as scheduled depends on the withdrawal of the Japanese army. It is expected that the Japanese army will withdraw outside the Guan within a month, at the earliest also in two weeks. As for the issue of the disposal of the puppet army, although the Japanese side has stated that it can be disposed of by our side, the difficult situation is not just one aspect. The other side can only not provide relief to this kind of army at the highest limit. If we want it to help us to resolve it by force, it will be difficult to do. In the future, even if we respond with force, but due to the relationship of the non-armed zone, sometimes the force is not enough, it can come and go freely, and it is difficult for us to respond. Before the Sino-Japanese issue is fully resolved, I am afraid that it will not be easy to put it out immediately. As of today, the 6th, the tracks of the Beining Road, Tangfang, and other stations have been repaired. The Luanhe Grand Iron Bridge has been repaired by the Japanese army and restored to its original state. If the puppet army issue can be resolved as soon as possible, the Beining Road train can reach Tangshan to the east, and the Pingyu transportation will be difficult to restore for a while. (June 6th)

Preliminary Preparations for the Establishment of the Political Affairs Commission 82

Likely to be Established in the Shortest Possible Time

Central Government Formulates Organizational Outline

Beiping Dispatch: Since Huang Fu was appointed to head the Beiping Political Affairs Reorganization Committee on the 17th of last month, nearly twenty days have passed. Initially, due to the military situation, pressing matters had to be addressed urgently, leaving no time for arranging committee affairs. The guests received daily were almost exclusively military or government personnel. Among the key figures, Huang Shaoxiong was frequently with He Yingqin discussing military matters, while Wang Kemin has been bedridden at Peking Union Medical College after injuring his eye a few days ago. Yu Xuezhong, Zhang Zhitian, Wang Yitang, Zhang Boling, and Wang Shuhan, who were in Tianjin, specifically came to Beiping to meet Tang Erhe. Liu Zhe, Lu Dangping, Song Zheyuan, and Fu Zuoyi also occasionally visited. Ding Wenjiang will soon head south, then proceed to the United States, and seemingly has no attention to committee affairs. Zhou Zuomin is in Shanghai urging his return, while Wang Boqun is ill in Shanghai. Li Shizeng, Zhang Puquan, and Enhe Batu are also not present. Han Fuqu and Xu Yongchang, due to their heavy duties as chairmen, will likely only come when meetings are necessary, although they maintain frequent contact and provide updates. As the ceasefire agreement concluded, North China is transitioning from military to political affairs, so the Political Affairs Commission is now actively preparing for its establishment in the short term.

Tracing the origins of the Political Affairs Commission, it evolved from the previous Political Subcommittee to the Political Affairs Committee under Zhang Hanqing. However, the Political Affairs Committee also included many military figures. With the establishment of the Military Affairs Subcommittee, military personnel, except for provincial chairmen, mostly belonged to the Military Affairs Subcommittee, and the Political Affairs Commission became a purely political organ. The Political Affairs Commission is responsible for reorganizing North China's political affairs and operates as a committee system. However, the organizational law emphasizes the chairman as the central figure, necessitating a precise internal organizational structure. Previously, there was a separate Finance Committee, which has now been merged into the Finance Department. The Political Affairs Commission also had departments for political affairs, confidential matters, and Mongolian and Tibetan affairs, which are now replaced by the Political Affairs Department. According to the organizational law, there are three departments: Political Affairs, Finance, and Secretariat. The Finance Department is the successor to the Finance Committee and is headed by Vice-Chairman Wang Kemin, so personnel matters are already settled. Wang Shuhan, head of the Political Affairs Department, previously came to Beiping, but departmental affairs are still under discussion. The Secretariat is central to the Political Affairs Commission's affairs, as Finance and Political Affairs deal with subordinate provinces and cities, while the Secretariat oversees all internal matters. Secretary-General He Qigong, who serves as the Mayor of Beiping, is very familiar with the local situation. During the organization, it is planned to divide the department into four sections: Documents, General Affairs, Public Relations, and Translation. The Councilors' Office is directly under the Committee, comprising all councilors, advisors, consultants, and specialists, whose main tasks are research, investigation, compilation, and review.

The Political Affairs Commission is the highest administrative organ of the Executive Yuan stationed in Beiping, governing four provinces and two cities, wielding significant power. However, it is an overarching body, with local authorities responsible for implementing measures. The commission merely issues directives, resolves doubts, and makes decisions. Its sole critical task lies in managing crises and uniting factions. From a direct perspective, it is respected but not intimately involved, while from a lateral perspective, it is both observed and respected. However, Chinese politics have always been fraught with factionalism and complex interpersonal relationships, making coordination and maneuvering difficult.

The Political Affairs Commission's location is currently being arranged in the west wing of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Once established, the various departments will move in. Before the formal establishment, a few individuals are handling affairs in Fengze Garden in Zhongnanhai, a former imperial palace. After the revolution, it belonged to the Presidential Palace, serving as a reception area or the office of the Secretary of State. After the Northern Expedition and the capital moved to Nanjing, it became a park and was fully opened to the public. The Zhongnanhai office was established here. When Huang Fu came to Beiping, it was used as his headquarters, conveniently located near He Yingqin's residence in Rentang Hall. Fengze Garden does not have many buildings. The front is Yinian Hall, and the back is Hanhe Hall. Before the commission is established, work is being done in the headquarters. This quiet old building is once again filled with guests, somewhat restoring its former glory.

The organizational outline of the Political Affairs Commission has been formulated and promulgated by the Central Government. The original text is as follows: Article 1: The Executive Yuan, to reorganize the political affairs of the northern provinces and cities, establishes the Executive Yuan's Political Affairs Reorganization Committee in Beiping. Article 2: The committee consists of 23 members, one of whom is designated as the chairman, selected by the President of the Executive Yuan and appointed by the National Government after approval by the Central Political Conference. Article 3: The chairman oversees the affairs of the committee. Article 4: The committee meets once a month, convened by the chairman. The rules of procedure are determined separately. The chairman may convene extraordinary meetings when necessary. Article 5: The committee establishes the following three departments: (1) Secretariat; (2) Political Affairs Department; (3) Finance Department. Article 6: The committee establishes one secretary-general to manage the affairs of the Secretariat, one director of political affairs to manage the affairs of the Political Affairs Department, and one director of finance to manage the affairs of the Finance Department. If necessary, each department may establish deputy directors. The detailed organizational rules are determined separately. Article 7: The committee may appoint councilors, advisors, and specialists as needed. Article 8: The committee may formulate separate regulations within the scope of not conflicting with central laws and regulations, submitting them to the Executive Yuan for approval and implementation. Article 9: The detailed rules of procedure for the committee are determined separately. Article 10: This provisional organizational outline takes effect from the date of promulgation. (6th)

Songjiang 83

Business Tax Levied on Lime and Brick Industry

The lime and brick kiln industry has historically operated with individual business permits and was therefore not subject to the general business tax. Now, the provincial government has promulgated special collection regulations for this industry, initially proposing a tax of 10% on net profits, later revised to 5%. Wu Xinren has been appointed as the Director of the Provincial Business Tax Bureau for this industry, dividing the province into eleven districts for separate collection. Songjiang, Fengxian, Jinshan, and Qingpu counties are grouped into one district, with a collection office established. An announcement was issued yesterday, requiring merchants in the industry to comply.

Suzhou 84

Xie Fengqi Dies Suddenly in Inn

Xie Fengqi, a 29-year-old man from Anhui residing on Hulong Street near Leqiao Doufen Garden, was formerly a revenue collector. This spring, he was introduced to the City Hotel by a friend to work as an external accountant, having deposited a cash pledge of 300 yuan. During the Dragon Boat Festival, the hotel suddenly dismissed Xie without fully returning his deposit, causing him to remain at the hotel, constantly distressed. On the evening of the 6th, he drank two catties of wine in room 15 and chatted happily with the waiter. Unexpectedly, he was found dead yesterday (7th) morning. The waiter, Rong Heshang, discovered Xie lying in a pool of blood with a deep and wide wound. He was rushed to Guangmin Hospital, but due to excessive blood loss, his life was in danger. The weapon used for the suicide, a large kitchen knife, was found under his pillow. Police officer Wang Xun and Xiang from the Second and Third Precincts have taken the case for record.

Father and Son Kidnapped in Chenmu Township 85

Gu Jinbiao, the head of Chenmu Township in Wuxian County, was attacked by over twenty bandits who broke into his home around 11 PM on the 6th. They robbed him of 500 yuan in cash, clothing, and other items. Gu Jinbiao and his seven-year-old son, A Xiao, were also taken away by the bandits, who fled towards Wanqiandang.

Wuxi 86

Crisis in the Revival of Sericulture

This year's spring silkworms were excellent, and farmers in the villages were overjoyed. The silk market also reached a peak, so farmers are mostly making plans for autumn planting. According to a recent survey, about two thousand sheets of silkworm eggs have been ordered near Yuqi Town, and less than half of the farmers have placed orders. It is expected that autumn planting sales will be three to four times higher than spring planting. Yesterday, the reporter visited Dong Shuzhen, director of the Dongcun Guidance Center, run by the county's agricultural farm. According to her, the amount of autumn silkworm eggs ordered by nearby farmers is several times greater than their own mulberry fields can support. Although this is a good sign that farmers are recovering from losses in silkworm production, there is concern that there will be too few mulberry leaves and too many silkworms, creating a great danger. Therefore, after investigating the amount of mulberry leaves available nearby, some restrictions should be imposed to avoid danger. It is hoped that the county agricultural farm and those concerned about the rural economy will pay attention to this.

Qingpu 87

Robbery of Nunnery and Rape of Nuns

Fushou Nunnery in Wang Village, south of Jinze in the county, has several nuns who accumulate savings through chanting scriptures and offering incense, making them a target for bandits. Around 7 PM the night before last, several bandits suddenly arrived, claiming to be there to request scripture chanting. They knocked on the door and entered, engaging in a large-scale robbery and forcibly raping nuns who were considered attractive. After the incident, it was discovered that seventy or eighty yuan had been stolen. The incident has been reported to the district regiment headquarters for investigation and arrest.

Nantong 88

Female Normal School Student Missing

Zong XX, a student in the second year of junior high school at the County Girls' Normal School, was falsely accused by her classmates. Ashamed and resentful, she left the school after leaving a suicide note on her pillow. The dormitory supervisor discovered this during room checks on the night of the 4th. The note stated that she could not withstand the pressure of the environment and would commit suicide by drowning. The school staff and the Public Security Bureau have been searching, but she has not been found.

Local News

New Currency from the Mint to Circulate 89

American Chief Technician Mr. Grand to Arrive in Shanghai Tomorrow

Review Committee to Begin Testing New Currency

Since the Central Mint began minting new currency, it has already produced over two million pieces. Various sectors are hoping to see the currency circulate soon. It is learned that the second review committee will meet tomorrow and begin testing the new currency. Mr. Grand, the newly hired American chief technician, is also scheduled to arrive in Shanghai tomorrow. It is reported that he will plan to reorganize China's currency system. Details are reported below:

Second Review Committee to Meet Tomorrow 90

After the New Currency Review Committee was established last month, it held its first meeting, deciding on the testing methods and other procedures. It is learned that the committee is eager to put the newly minted currency into circulation as soon as possible. Therefore, the second committee meeting was originally scheduled for yesterday afternoon to conduct testing. However, due to many committee members having other important official duties, it was postponed to 4 PM tomorrow (9th) at the Central Bank's third floor. At that time, inspection and testing will begin. One or two coins will be selected from every ten thousand coins for testing. If they meet the prescribed standards, they will be approved for circulation nationwide.

American Chief Technician to Arrive in Shanghai Tomorrow 91

The Central Mint originally had a foreign chief technician named Li Weide, but he resigned and returned to his country due to old age. Finance Minister Song Ziwen specially hired Mr. Grand, a renowned American minting expert, to Shanghai to fill the position. Mr. Grand has served as the director of various mints in the United States and has extensive experience. He arrived in Shanghai on May 19th aboard the Dollar Steamship Lines' President Coolidge and is scheduled to arrive tomorrow. It is reported that Mr. Grand has a plan to reorganize China's currency system, which will be implemented by the financial authorities.

Minting Process is Quite Complex 92

The silver used by the mint is melted down from large thousand-tael bars collected from various banks in Shanghai. First, it is tested and mixed with pure electrolytic copper, then melted into small hundred-yuan bars and rolled into thin sheets using a rolling machine. Then, they are stamped into round blanks, and finally, patterns are stamped using steel molds. Each time it goes through a machine, it must be baked and washed. Therefore, the minting of one silver dollar requires a very complex process. Finally, after being inspected by the review committee, it is circulated on the market. Currently, an average of 200,000 silver dollars can be produced per day. The composition is approximately 88% pure silver and 12% copper, melted together. The coins produced daily are sent to the Central Bank for storage in preparation for issuance.

Japanese Envoy Akira Ariyoshi Enters Beijing Yesterday 100

Claims to Visit Various Authorities of the National Government

Does Not Involve Sino-Japanese Political Issues

Whether to Go to Beiping is Still Undecided

The Japanese Ambassador to China, Akira Ariyoshi, accompanied by his wife, Counselor and Mrs. Ariyoshi, Secretary Horiuchi, and Mrs. Okazaki, a total of six people, boarded a private car C502 and attached it to the express train departing from Shanghai to Beijing at 10 AM yesterday morning. Approximately 30 people, including Japanese Embassy Secretary Okazaki, Information Director Suma, and Japanese residents, went to the North Station to see them off. The Public Security Bureau of the Fifth District dispatched many armed police officers, together with the road police, to protect the station. The Municipal Government also sent Secretary Wang Changchun to see them off. According to Ariyoshi's statement to Japanese reporters before his departure, his trip to Beijing was to visit various authorities of the National Government and tour Nanjing. He would not engage in any negotiations on Sino-Japanese political issues. He planned to stay in Beijing for two or three days and then return to Shanghai. Whether to go to Beiping was still undecided. At the same time, Secretary Okazaki, who went to see him off, said that the ambassador's trip had no political relationship. A reporter from the New News Agency learned from reliable sources yesterday that Ariyoshi's sudden entry into Beijing was indeed due to a secret order from the Foreign Ministry of his country. His important task was to raise a request to our diplomatic authorities in a private capacity regarding the new tariffs promulgated by our country on May 12 and the anti-dumping taxes to be levied, as the Japanese side believed that after the customs announced the new tariffs, Japanese goods exported to China would be severely hit.

Ministry of Communications Borrows Boxer Indemnity Funds to Purchase New Telegraph Machines from England 101

Sixteen Creed Machines and Four Printing Machines

To be Shipped Soon to Various Bureaus for Application

The Ministry of Communications believes that most of the telegraph machines used by China's telegraph bureaus are Morse and Hughes, both of which are very fast, but the receiving procedure is cumbersome and slow. Therefore, European and American countries have recently abandoned them and use Creed high-speed telegraph machines. Due to economic reasons, China has not been able to replace them until now. In order to develop the business of various telegraph bureaus and strive for improvement, the ministry has borrowed £10,000 from the China Boxer Indemnity Board and a portion of the water conservancy project funds to purchase sixteen Creed machines and four Inker machines from England. The negotiations have been completed, and the machines will soon be shipped and assigned to telegraph bureaus in Nanjing, Shanghai, Hankou, Beiping, Qingdao, Yantai, and other places for application.

This City will Begin Collecting Land Value Tax 102

Collection Scope Limited to the Chinese Area

According to the Central News Agency, the collection of land value tax in this city has been in preparation since the municipal government submitted it to the central government for approval, and a preparatory committee for the collection of land value tax was established. It has been several months, but the Executive Yuan believes that the draft regulations for the collection of land value tax originally proposed by the municipal government still need to be amended, so the preparatory work of the committee has been suspended invisibly. It is learned that the regulations have been approved by the Executive Yuan meeting on the 6th. The reporter specifically asked Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, about this matter. According to him, the Executive Yuan's approval has not yet been received. As soon as the approval is received, preparations will continue, and it is planned to complete the preparatory work and begin collection in a few days. The collection scope is limited to the Chinese area and will be carried out district by district. The survey of the French Concession and other districts of Shanghai has been completed, so the Concession and other districts will start collection first.

Finnish Aviator to Fly to Qingdao This Morning 103

The Shanghai Times reported that Finnish aviator Captain Bai Limai flew from Hong Kong to Shanghai yesterday morning (6th) at 5:40 AM. After stopping briefly in Xiamen at 10 AM to refuel, he continued his journey. He encountered headwinds along the way, so he could have arrived at the Hongqiao Airport at 3 PM in the afternoon, but he was delayed until 5:15 PM, flying 500 miles in seven and a half hours. When he departed from Hong Kong, he was thinly dressed. The temperature dropped sharply along the way, and he encountered strong winds, so he felt very cold. After landing and arranging his plane, he and Mr. Salimen, the Finnish acting consul-general in Shanghai who welcomed him at the scene, took a car to Mr. Sa's residence on Groisy Road in the French Concession. Captain Bai departed from Helsinki, the capital of Finland, on May 11th. He stayed in Berlin for 10 days, then passed through Hungary and Turkey to enter Persia, and then flew through India, Bangkok, and the estuary to Hong Kong. This trip is for pleasure and has the purpose of promoting Finland. Mr. Bai previously served in the Finnish Air Force. Last year, he flew alone from the Finnish capital to Cape Town, South Africa, and then flew back, becoming famous in the world. The Ta Mei Evening News reported that Captain Bai Limai is scheduled to fly to Qingdao tomorrow morning, and then take the road through Korea to Japan.

The Red Swastika Society Reports Tragic News of Disaster-Stricken Children in Shaanxi 116

The Shanghai General Office of the World Red Swastika Society received a letter from the relief commissioner yesterday, reporting the tragic plight of disaster-stricken children. It is too painful to read. The original letter is transcribed below: "The two previous letters have hopefully reached you. Chairmen Li and Wang of the Dong and Ri Associations have both returned from relief efforts in the western region, remitting 10,000 yuan in relief funds, which has been received. It is planned to continue relief efforts in the Xiapifeng and Wugong counties in the western region, and to establish a disaster relief and care center in Liquan. Refugees in the province are 80% women and children, mostly from counties in the western region. They have lost their homes and their parents have died in ditches. Young children, barely weaned, wander the streets, each holding a small tin can, begging from door to door. On average, they cannot beg even ten copper coins a day. When hungry, they eat onion roots and sorghum stalks. When thirsty, they drink cold water like cattle. It is very difficult to get a bowl of noodle soup. At night, they sleep on the streets, exposed to the elements. It is feared that few will survive this hot summer. We hope that charitable organizations will come to Shaanxi as soon as possible to rescue these disaster-stricken children. The merit of this work cannot be compared to the relief of wounded soldiers.

代徵漁業建設費 126

The Attempt to Collect Fishing Industry Construction Fees 127

Mediation Failed Yesterday

Government and Merchants Persist

Further Discussions This Afternoon

The Fishery Construction Fee Collection Office of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Area Fishery Improvement Committee of the Ministry of Industries, because it forced fish businesses to collect fees on its behalf, aroused dissatisfaction among the majority of members of the Fresh Fish Trade Association of this city, who unanimously denied responsibility for collecting the fees on behalf of the committee. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Yu Zhiqing, Du Yuesheng, Yu Zuoting, and Hu Diansun gathered fishery administration personnel and fish business managers at the 4th floor of the Ningbo Fellow Townsmen Association to discuss mediation. Because both sides persisted in their views, the mediation failed. The detailed situation is recorded below:

Attendees 128

The attendees included Yu Qiaqing, Du Yuesheng, Yu Zuoting, Hu Diansun, Fang Jiaobo, Zhang Shenzhi, Chen Zhongsheng, Zhou Jianyin, Director of the Fishery Administration Bureau, Lin Kanghou, Section Chief of the Fisheries and Animal Husbandry Department of the Ministry of Industries, and 22 fish business managers from this city, including Zhang Zhenfang and Liu Tonghua. Several hundred fishermen and fish business associates who came to Shanghai to sell fish, and Mao Anqing and Le Badong, representatives from the Dunshou Public Office of the Ningbo Fish Business, were also present. After 3:00 PM, both sides arrived and the mediation began.

Mediation Situation 129

First, Mr. Yu reported the reasons for convening the mediation meeting. Then, he asked each fish business manager for their opinions. Yu Zuoting and Hu Diansun, representing the fish business managers, stated the reasons for the difficulty of collecting construction fees on behalf of the fish businesses, saying that most transactions between fish businesses and fishermen are on credit. The fishermen are unwilling to pay the construction fee, and the fish businesses are not in a position to force them to pay. If the fish businesses were to force them to pay, the fishermen would be making the payment against their will, and the fish businesses' credit accounts would be difficult to collect. Naturally, the result would be that the fish businesses would be paying the construction fee on behalf of the fishermen. Zhou Jianyin then stated the reasons why the construction fee must be collected on behalf of the fish businesses, saying that the order for the fish businesses to collect the construction fee on behalf of the committee was set by the ministry. If the fish businesses were not responsible for collecting the fee on behalf of the committee, it would be equivalent to overturning the collection of the construction fee.

Proposal for Consideration 130

Mr. Zhou also stated that if the fish businesses were not responsible for collecting the construction fee on behalf of the committee, the collection office would have no choice but to detain all goods for which the construction fee had not been paid in the future and enforce the collection. Each fish business manager stated that because of their own interests, they would rather close shop and cease operations than collect the construction fee on behalf of the committee, thus incurring the cost of the construction fee for no reason. At this point in the mediation, because both sides insisted on their views, it was considered hopeless. Mr. Yu stood up and said that this matter was of great importance and should be considered carefully. It was then decided that this afternoon would be the deadline for a final decision, and the meeting was adjourned.

The Shanghai Domestic Products Manufacturers Association, intending to exhibit the products of various factories, requested the Ministry of Industries to issue tax exemption certificates and reduced freight vouchers. Please forward them to the Ningbo County Government for use in the exhibition and transport of domestic products. Enclosed are two copies of the certificate and freight voucher filling methods. Please forward them to be followed and reported. This order, etc.," which was printed and filed. The telegram was sent to inform. The association, after receiving the approval and attachments, has sent the tax exemption certificate and reduction vouchers to the Domestic Products Manufacturers Association for verification and receipt.

Reasons for Demanding the Cancellation of Awning Fees 132

Thieler Agrees to Submit to the Board of Directors for Discussion

The Second Special District Citizens' Association previously sent several letters to the Municipal Council regarding the French Concession's collection of awning fees, requesting cancellation. However, the French Municipal Council has not responded. The association requested the Director of the Public Relations Department, Zhai Zhenhua, to go to the French Municipal Council to negotiate with Director Thieler and present two reasons: (1) Awnings are used for a very short time and do not obstruct pedestrians, so they should not be used to collect fees. (2) Although there was previously this fee, it was only 20 cents per quarter. This time, the fees are as high as 4 to 5 yuan. In this time of economic depression, merchants and citizens cannot afford to pay. Director Thieler accepted the above two points and agreed to submit them to the Board of Directors for discussion and to develop a sound solution.

The Corpse Was Collected by the Shop Owner

Former New World Tea Server Extorts Money from Inspector 138

Shen Guanghua (also known as Gangzi), a Jiangbei native residing at No. 4664 Robert's Road in West Shanghai, used to work as a tea server at the New World Amusement Park. He often disagreed with Wang Songfu, an inspector from Nanjing at the park. During the Lunar New Year this year, New World reopened, but Shen's business was suddenly terminated. Suspecting that Wang had instigated this, his resentment deepened, and he thought of revenge. On the Dragon Boat Festival, Shen invited four accomplices to ambush Wang Songfu at the intersection of Jiujiang Road and Xizang Road. They swarmed forward, blocked his path, and assaulted him with fists and feet. As a result, Wang suffered minor injuries, and his clothes were torn. Shen and the others scattered and fled. However, Wang initially intended to pursue the matter, but Shen's relative, Dong Shuangquan, who served as a headman in the fire brigade, repeatedly mediated with Wang, and the matter was dropped. Unexpectedly, Shen was still unwilling to let it go. At 10:30 AM the day before yesterday, he wrote a threatening letter and mailed it to Wang. The letter contained strong language, recounting the facts of his termination and demanding that Wang compensate him for the loss of his job. He gave Wang two days to reply. If he did not comply, he would take further action. After receiving the letter, Wang reported it to the Xinzha police station, which dispatched detectives Ye Yushan and Dong Shuangquan to investigate Shen's whereabouts. Shen Guanghua was found at the rooftop garden of the New New Company. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Jiang Baolian explained the case, stating that according to Article 319 of the Criminal Law on obstructing freedom, the defendant Shen Guanghua was being prosecuted. Wang Songfu, the plaintiff, also testified to the previous events. When questioned, the defendant's testimony was evasive. After a court-appointed public defender and the police lawyer presented their arguments, Judge Liu Yugui reviewed the evidence and announced that the debate in the case was concluded and that the verdict would be announced on Friday of this week.

Prostitute Strives to Escape the Sea of Suffering 139

丨Accuses Madame of Obstructing Freedom丨

Lin Yaqin, also known as A Si, a woman from Haimen, is currently twenty-three years old. When she was twelve, her hometown was devastated by floods, and Lin's entire family was scattered without a trace. Alone and lonely, she encountered kidnappers who lured her to Shanghai and sold her to Madame Yang Ajin. Yang opened a brothel in Fuxiang Lane. Seeing that Lin was beautiful, she instructed her to learn to sing and play musical instruments, preparing her to solicit customers in the future. At the age of fourteen, Lin's training was complete, and Yang forced her into prostitution, changing her name to Wang Baobao. From then on, she was busy with soliciting customers and had no free time. If she slightly disobeyed, she would be frequently beaten and suffered greatly. In 1931, Yang moved her business to Fuyu Lane, renaming herself Xia Jun. Later, because the prostitution business was poor, Yang sold Lin to Feng Deming as a concubine for 1,200 yuan. Lin thought that she could finally regain her freedom and escape the fire pit. Unexpectedly, fate was fickle. Feng was deeply addicted to gambling and had no profession, so he was unable to maintain a living. Feng and Yang Ajin agreed to redeem Lin for 205 yuan. In the spring of this year, she was transferred to Yaqin Brothel in Fuyu Lane as a prostitute for 150 yuan. Before long, the business declined, and Yaqin Brothel closed. Yang then changed her approach and forced Lin to solicit customers at various amusement parks, a practice commonly known as "tangbai." From then on, she engaged in the flesh trade, and her suffering deepened. Over the years, the income from her nightly fees was considerable, and all the clothes and jewelry given by customers were taken and stored by Yang. Lin received not a penny. Resentful, she often thought of escaping the cage and escaping the sea of suffering, but Yang was very vigilant, and there was no opportunity. It wasn't until last month that she finally seized an opportunity to escape. She went to Lawyer Xiong Fei for help, requesting him to find a way to break her relationship with Yang, restore her personal freedom, and return the clothes and jewelry given by customers. Lawyer Xiong immediately sent a letter to Yang questioning her. Unexpectedly, Yang not only refused to return them but also claimed that Lin owed more than a thousand yuan in debt and could only be free after the debt was cleared. Lin had no choice but to ask Lawyer Xiong to file a complaint with the First Special District Court, accusing Yang Ajin of obstructing her freedom and attaching a civil suit, requesting a judgment to return the clothes and jewelry worth 553 yuan. The court approved the request and ordered a summons for yesterday afternoon. Judge Qian Wenji presided over the joint interrogation in the Second Criminal Court. Because the address of Yang written in the original complaint was 837 Fuhua Lane, Pike Road, she could not be found. Therefore, the defendant did not appear. Judge Qian briefly questioned Lin Yaqin and ordered the case to be rescheduled, pending the arrival of the defendant for further questioning.

Young Swindler Refreshes His Wardrobe in a Flash 140

Taking Care Earnestly in the Name of Fellow Villager

A Look Back and the Wicker Trunk Was Gone

Wu Xiao, a forty-year-old woman from Anhui province, came to Shanghai for business and stayed at the Fuxin Hotel in the French Concession. She became acquainted with a young man who lived nearby. The young man claimed to be a fellow villager of Xiao, so they became even closer. The day before yesterday evening, Xiao purchased some cloth and several items of her own clothing, which she stored in a wicker trunk, preparing to take a boat back home. The young man learned of this and volunteered to carry the trunk and accompany her to board the ship, fulfilling the obligation of a fellow villager. When they reached the gangway of the Shun Ferry at the Jinliyuan Wharf of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Xiao turned around and saw that the young man had disappeared. Xiao was anxious because the cash and clothing in the trunk were worth about a hundred yuan. She immediately returned to the original hotel to inquire about his whereabouts. After a while, the young man did return, but he had changed into a new silk long gown, a new straw hat, and new maoge shoes, looking completely different from before. The wicker trunk was gone. Xiao immediately grabbed him and called the police, who took him to the police station. Since the case occurred on the water, the Maritime Customs Police Station was notified, and Detective Shen Changshan brought the plaintiff and defendant back for questioning. According to the defendant, who identified himself as Chen Zhenghuan, a twenty-five-year-old man from Anhui, the clothing and other items in the plaintiff's wicker trunk had all been pawned off to buy clothes for his use. He still had ten yuan left. The police chief immediately ordered him to be sent to court for trial.

Page 12

Apprentice Fight Leads to Death, Shop Owner Conceals Report 141

Refrigerating the Corpse with a Large Block of Ice

Police Station Investigates Relevant Persons Based on Reports

At 6:00 PM the day before yesterday, an apprentice fight occurred on Gonghe Road in Zhabei, leading to a death and concealment of the body, attempting to destroy the case. The Fourth District Public Security Bureau and the Detective Team discovered this yesterday afternoon. The details are recorded below:

Gonghe Road Giant Store 142

The Gonghechun Wine and Noodle Restaurant is located at No. 53 Gonghe Road in Zhabei. It is a double-fronted store that has been in business for several years and has a very good business, making it a giant store on Gonghe Road. The owner is a Mr. Xu from Wuxi, who passed away several years ago. All store affairs are now managed by his son, Xu Fengqi. Most of the shop assistants are also hired from Wuxi, including two apprentices: one named San Nv, nineteen years old, with an unknown surname, and one named Han Xi Nv, seventeen years old, also from Wuxi. They specialize in delivering noodles at the restaurant.

A Punch to the Temple 143

Around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday (the 6th), the two apprentices suddenly started arguing, and the dispute escalated to a physical fight. They exchanged punches and kicks. However, Han Ding Nv was slightly younger and not as strong as San Nv. He was punched in the temple by San Nv, and Xi Nv immediately fell to the ground. San Nv attempted to add to the assault, but fortunately, the other shop assistants intervened and stopped San Nv. They told Xi Nv to get up on his own. However, Xi Nv's face was pale, and his breathing was weak. They thought he had been hit in the chest and was unable to breathe, or that he was dizzy from the blow. They quickly helped him up, carried him upstairs, and laid him on the bed, covering him with blankets to let him rest.

Sleeping Never to Wake 144

After a while, the other shop assistants became worried because Xi Nv had been sleeping silently for a long time. They asked San Nv to go upstairs with them to check on him. They saw that Xi Nv's face had turned gray and he had no breath. They felt him and he was ice-cold. He had been dead for a long time. The shop assistants were shocked and immediately reported to the young owner, Xu Fengqi. Upon hearing the news, Xu was terrified because the matter involved a death. He quickly discussed solutions with the other assistants. At the same time, Xu was afraid of being implicated himself, so he secretly instructed the other assistants to keep the matter a secret. He then secretly purchased a large amount of ice and refrigerated Xi Nv's body with ice in order to find another way to deal with it.

Police Station Investigation 145

Unexpectedly, the matter was not kept secret and was heard by neighbors. At 5:00 PM yesterday afternoon, they secretly reported it to the Fourth District Headquarters. District Chief Lai received the report and immediately dispatched Detective Foremen Wang Shifu and Geng Shoubao, Detectives Miao Jinhai, Fang Chaozu, Wang Songlin, Zhao Huai'ren, and Xu Jingen, and Patrol Officer Mu Chengjin, leading officers to investigate the truth at the restaurant. They indeed discovered a corpse. There was a bruise on the temple of the head. They questioned each shop assistant individually and learned the above details. They immediately arrested San Nv and brought the young owner and the old boss's wife to the headquarters for detention. They also instructed the local bailiff to guard the corpse at the noodle restaurant and reported it to the court for inspection today. After the discovery of this matter, those who came to watch the scene were extremely crowded. When the trial opens in the future, it will likely cause a sensation among tens of thousands of people.

Large-Scale Raid on Opium Dens in the French Concession 146

Over One Hundred Opium Pipes

Two Hundred Opium Addicts, Male and Female

Recently, opium pills have become prevalent in the market. Due to the high price of raw opium, most people in the underworld have switched to opium pills. As a result, those addicted to opium pills account for eight out of ten, while those who smoke opium only account for two out of ten. Currently, the two most popular types of opium pills are the "Eleventh Hour" and "Taixing" brands. Opium pill dens (commonly known as "zizi ke") are most numerous on Zilaihuo Street in the French Concession, in Ruifu Lane. The French Chief Inspector learned of this and immediately dispatched a large number of French, Vietnamese, and Chinese detectives and police officers, totaling several hundred, to surround Ruifu Lane yesterday (the 7th) at around 10:00 AM. The Western Detective Chief personally led the Chinese and Western detectives to search house by house. After three hours, they seized three opium pipes, over one hundred opium pill pipes, and countless opium lamps and smoking paraphernalia. They arrested over two hundred people, including den owners and opium addicts, male and female (because the fingers of those who smoke opium pills inevitably turn yellow, the fingers of those arrested were inspected and there was no way to hide it). They filled seven trucks and sent them in batches to the Dazimingzhong Police Station for separate detention and investigation. Since this large-scale raid, the scourge of opium pills in the French Concession may be somewhat curbed.

Bloodshed on Xiaoshadu Road 150

Sudden Attack While Sound Asleep

The Yin Lianzi Couple Severely Injured

Yin Lianzi, from Yancheng, is thirty years old. He is married to Zhang, who is twenty-four years old, also from Yancheng. Yin works as a teahouse attendant in the Jiangbei Theater on Xiaoshadu Road. Their home is at No. 5 Fuyuan Lane, Xiaoshadu Road. At around 3:10 AM yesterday morning, while the Yin couple was sound asleep, several thugs broke open the back door of the house and rushed directly to Yin's bedroom upstairs. They took out sharp blades and slashed wildly at Yin and Zhang. The two were wounded and were awakened from their dreams, screaming for help. The thugs were caught and quickly went downstairs to escape. Neighbors arrived to find the couple lying in a pool of blood. They immediately reported to the Gordon Road Police Station, which dispatched patrol officer No. 2451 to the scene. The two injured people were transported to Renji Hospital for treatment. Yin was the most seriously injured, with about six or seven cuts to the head and two cuts to both feet. Yin's wife, Zhang, only had one cut to the head. The identity of the perpetrators is unknown because it was dark. However, according to Zhang, someone had previously asked Yin for money unsuccessfully, and this may have been an act of revenge. The Gordon Road Police Station is still investigating.

Departments for Tuberculosis, Nervous Disorders, and General Cases Established

Officially Admits Patients Starting on the 15th of This Month

Trial and Verdict of Case Involving Enticement of Communists to Surrender and Incitement to Strike 154

丨Ding and Yu Each Fined 20 Yuan丨

Ding Zhiyi and Yu Jun, secret agents from the Supervisory Office of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, learned that Tian Fuyuan, a worker at the Public Concession Telephone Company, was nominally registered as a communist and persuaded him to surrender. They scheduled a negotiation at a tea room near the Continental Marketplace on Jiujiang Road. When Ding and Yu went to fulfill the appointment, a conflict suddenly arose. Tian accused Ding and Yu of instigating him to incite his colleagues to strike, but because he refused, Ding and others tried to kidnap him. He called the police, who arrested them and took them to the police station. The next day, they were transferred to the First Special District Court for trial. The two sides attacked each other. Tian said that Ding and Yu instigated the strike, while Ding and Yu said that Tian was a communist. The judge ordered the original defendant and defendant to post bail separately and await further investigation. After a detailed investigation by the Chinese and Western detectives handling the case, it was confirmed that Ding Zhiyi and Yu Jun interfered with Tian Fuyuan's freedom of movement. Regardless of whether they had orders from superiors, they had crossed the border to make an arrest. Such illegal actions cannot be tolerated. Yesterday morning, the two defendants, Ding and Yu, were brought to the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Ru Bao'yi explained the police's findings, and Tian Fuyuan also came to court to explain the situation at the time. Ding and Yu insisted on their previous statements. After hearing the case, Judge Qian Hongye found that the defendants' statements were unsubstantiated and unreliable. He immediately pronounced the verdict, fining Ding and Yu 20 yuan each as a warning.

Customs Notice Redefines Navigation Jargon for Vessels 155

China Merchants Bureau Orders All Ship Captains to Comply

Collision or Violation Will Result in Fines

The Jianghai Customs, based on the International Maritime Conference, has redefined the navigation jargon for vessels and issued a notice to the China Merchants Bureau, ordering ship captains to comply. The notice states: "For compliance, according to the Customs Notice, the driving jargon has been redefined in accordance with the International Maritime Conference. From now on, all Logbooks and regular jargon must use RightLeft, and portStarboard must not be used. In the future, if a collision occurs due to violations, the violating party will inevitably lose the lawsuit. Therefore, the responsibility of the driver is very important and must be paid special attention to. The explanation of the new jargon is as follows: (A) If the ship's bow is to be turned to the left, everything is left. 1. The command is in English, the captain's command is Left. 2. The helmsman replies Left, the rudder wheel Wheel is turned to the left. 3. The pointer Pointer moves to the left. 4. The rudder Rudder moves to the left. 5. The ship's bow moves to the left. (B) If the ship's bow is to be turned to the right, everything is right. 1. The command is in English, the captain's command is Right. 2. The helmsman replies Right, the rudder wheel Wheel is turned to the right. 3. The pointer Pointer moves to the right. 4. The rudder Rudder moves to the right. 5. The ship's bow moves to the right. This order urgently notifies all ship captains to comply and to instruct the drivers to comply as a whole. This is very important. Do not make any mistakes."
